This marks the first ever State team championship for Maui Preparatory Academy, the

decades, when Lahainaluna won the title in 1982.

Madam Clerk, please proceed with testimony.
COUNTY CLERK: Chair, Members of the public may testify in the Council Chambers.
CHAIR LEE: We can barely hear you.
COUNTY CLERK: Okay, sorry. Members of the public may testify in the Council Chambers,
at courtesy testimony sites, or remotely through the information listed on the meeting
agenda.
Individuals in the Chamber may sign up to testify with the staff member located at the
desk in the 8th floor lobby. Individuals at the courtesy testimony sites may sign up with
the staff member at the site. Individuals participating remotely may also sign up in the
meeting chat. If you are connected to the meeting by phone, you'll automatically be
added to the testifier list.
Individuals connected by phone are currently on mute and will be unmuted when it is
their time to testify. Individuals connected by video conference should keep both their
video and microphones off and should turn them on only when it is their time to testify.
Testimony is limited to the items listed on the agenda. And individuals may testify for
up to three minutes per item. When testifying, please state your name and the name
of any organization you represent, as well as the items on which you will be testifying.
Please also identify to the Council if you are a paid lobbyist.
After your testimony has concluded, please disconnect from BlueJeans. Once the
testimony period is closed, only the Councilmembers, staff, and designated resource
persons will be connected to the meeting. All other individuals will be disconnected.
The remainder of the meeting can be viewed on Akaku Maui Community Media,
Channel 53, or on mauicounty.legistar.com. Individuals may also be disconnected
from the public hearing, from the meeting at any time for breaking decorum.
Chair, the first person to testify is Donna Hansen. To be followed by Bob Hansen.
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui

PRESENTATION OF ORAL TESTIMONY
MS. DONNA HANSEN (testifying on Committee Report No. 22-41):
Good morning. Hello. This is, what, what am I doing?
MR. BOB HANSEN: Geez, hold on. Hold on one second.
MS. HANSEN: Sorry.
CHAIR LEE: What happened there?
MR. HANSEN: Okay, go.
MS. HANSEN: Apologies. I'm sorry.
CHAIR LEE: No problem.
MS. HANSEN: I'm Donna Hansen. I represent myself, and this is about Resolution 22-70.
My statement is Maui's citizens, like other islands and States, have endured over two
years of turbulent experience. During this time, you have passed several laws that
have caused even more problems. These taxes and laws are driving the local citizens
out, favoring the hotel industry and more affluent visitors. We are trying, we are finally
experiencing the fine, the beginning of a recuperation for restaurants, retail and
businesses, even though some of your tax bills and other laws have caused much
harm.
However, through these decisions, the County has gained a financial surplus by pulling
even more tax dollars from the public, which my understanding was assisting, was for
assisting the population who requires many needs such as housing, etc.
Congratulations on creating a surplus for the County. But because of this surplus, each
and every one of you has gained economic growth through large raises from the
Council, for the Council and other parts of the County, while the little people have
actually diminished in their spending ability due not only to inflation, but to taxes,
legislation.
Now, you have, sorry. I'm nervous. Now you have the new hurt the people bill, I believe,
by trying to control tourism accommodation growth, which assists the hotels and not
the mom-and-pop vacation renters. And rumor that it is because you guys favor the
hotels. And many of those are owned by foreign people, and not, and companies,
rather than by private people. I feel that that's really, really wrong.
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 12
I'm going to beg you to not crush Maui's economy further. And I would love it if you
would work toward bringing aloha spirit back to this island, because it is diminishing
constantly. You may not be aware of it, and I know you all are well-intentioned. But
you are blindsided by so many things that you have caused the little people on this
island. Please consider this very, very carefully, and not hurt us anymore. Thank you.
CHAIR LEE: Thank you.
May we have the next speaker?

Aloha, Council team. Nice to see you again. Nick Drance here testifying from the East

I ask the Council to support 22-70, because in so doing they cooperate with the
administrative functioning of County government. And a vote against that resolution
prevents the normal functioning of County government. Let the Planning Commission
and their advisory committees make the determinations and let the system and the
process move forward.
As far as the subject itself goes, you all know how I feel, Councilmember Johnson's
comments this, this morning about stewardship taking a big picture view of things is

on earth, what are we going to look back on? And  Ithink preservation and stewardship
are going to be the thing, the only things really that matter. And anything related to

MR. MIKE MORAN. KIHEI COMMUNITY ASSOCIATION ftestifvina on Bill Nos. 77 (2022)
and 78 (2022)1:
Happy Earth Day, Chair and Councilmembers. Mike Moran for the Kihei Community
Association. An appropriate day to be supporting Bill 77 and 78 for the pio, piokeo [sic]
watershed. And KCA had, did our best to dissuade development of that land for well
over a decade in trying to keep it open. So, this looks like the ultimate outcome that
we would want. And in that same area. I'll try not to dis, to sway too much from the
agenda, but after your closeout at yesterday's meeting, I was down by the shoreline,
and I thought sure I heard the few remaining corals cheering. I'm not sure. But maybe
it was that hallucination, but I think I did. And maybe they'll be cheering louder today
as this proceeds.
I would like to inject, cause sometimes we are asked why we're testifying on something
in, in Maalaea, as most of us refer to that general area, when we are the Kihei
Community Association. And historically, KCA was officially incorporated in 1960,
which may be before us, some guys here were born. But even before 1960, there was
a grassroots group, at least in the 50's that was an unofficial KCA. And when they
were getting things established, they were looking at all of South Maui, which of course
was much different then. There was no Maalaea Boat Harbor. There was no Kihei
Boat Harbor. All . . . right there in North Kihei, across from where these guys were,
were getting, were established, and there was a store there, and people said, oh yeah,
the Suda Store. No, this was the store before the Suda Store.
And they just, they chose the name Kihei because most people weren't looking so
much at other areas. So, that's in our bible, is that we speak for, our best for all of
South Maui. And now that other organizations have popped up over the last 60 years.

we concentrate more. But that's ... as our responsibility to speak up for South Maui,
and we, that this will be, will, will proceed, these two bills. And we can do wonders
again. It's really appropriate for Earth Day, if we can start doing something to help
Maaiaea Bay in its dire straits right now. So, as one of the little people, we think you
guys are doing a great job and thank you for all the good work you do. Aloha.

Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 18
the budget as the Mayor has suggested, to put in this extra little push of funds for the
Maalaea Mauka, Pohakea, also known as Pohakea Watershed areas.
These are very, very important land, if we are to bring back the health of Maalaea Bay,
which was once known as one of the most remarkable places for varieties of limu, and
for varieties of the little critters they call them gastropods. But all the little critters that
live in the reefs, and along the shoreline, that we find their beautiful shells along the
beach. This was a famous place for shells. In fact, folks would go in the 1960's and
1970's and just gather shells and make little shell art houses with them. This is one of
the prime places that families would go. This was kind of a trend among crafty ladies
in the 60's and 70's.
So, we need to bring back that abundance and the first step is managing the sediment
load, which is tremendous, that flows into our oceans from these upslope lands. It can
be done. It will be done. There's a plan for it to be done. All we need to do is actually
have one entity, the State in partnership with nonprofit organizations, like Maui Nui
Marine Resource Council, Sierra Club, the Maalaea Village Association, and others.
Soil and Water Conservation Districts, to manage that land. So, mahalo for your
support of these bills.
We'd also like to testify in support of Bill 76, which brings relief to our Upcountry farmers
for feral animal control. Anything we can do to make things easier for our farmers and
ranchers, not to be decimated by the unchecked populations of feral animals, we need
to do. This, this problem is so crazy that homeowners just don't bother planting
anything unless they can afford a fence, a big fence, because these deer can jump.
So, thank you for your support of that.
We're also supporting, in support of item 22-39, which sends a letter out to our Federal
representatives supporting regulations of the, the tour and helicopter flights. We call it
flight scene. They, they are a needed part of our economy. But they need to play fair,
and they should not target residential neighborhoods where the noise levels can
become unbearable. And I know the folks in Waikapu are very concerned about this.
And some of the folks Upcountry as well. It used to be a big problem out in Hueio
where we live. They came every half hour on the half hour. It was like living in Vietnam.
But through Federal interventions, there were regulations put in place. This is round
two. So, we, we thank you for your support on that.
Also, we would like to speak on item 22-97 and 22-40. Now, these are the amendments
to kind of have a reality check for what happens in this public, very needed public-
private partnership with the Waikapu Town Development. Sierra Club has testified in
support of this development because of its many green characteristics, including
dedicating 800 acres of agricultural land as a perpetual easement, as a buffer around

MR. DAVID DORN (testifying on Committee Report No. 22-41):
Hello? Konnichiwa and Happy Earth Day. My name is David Dorn, I'm not a lobbyist.
I agree with Lucienne on all her points. We do need to provide extra funding to protect
the Maalaea Watershed. And we need to support our Upcountry farmers to better
control feral animals in the mauka watershed.
I also support the adoption of Resolution 22-70. We need more homes, not hotels.
And we need to manage tourism so that it benefits Maui County locals, the moms and
pops. Maui County already has more than enough hotel rooms, time-shares and other
transient accommodations. We have more hotel rooms per capita than Oahu. And we
are more tourist dense than Waikiki. Maui now is up to one tourist for every two to
three locals, far exceeding our limits and our levels set in the Maui Island Plan. This is
totally unsustainable. There's not even enough locals to work these hotels. So, hotels
are importing more people to work in these hotels. Hotel work, workers are brought in
from the mainland and they are buying up our workforce and affordable housing. And
there is nothing to stop them.
The two-year visitor moratorium is actually benefiting the housing industry as
construction is focusing on home building and other kinds of construction. This is
actually helping us fill the need for more housing for locals. But this is only a temporary
solution to Maui's housing crisis. This bill for capping tourist accommodations could
similarly help our construction industry and the folks and the kind of projects that will
actually benefit local families, such as building more housing and schools.
Many hotels on Maui are owned by huge mainland corporation. A majority of profits
from the hotel goes offshore to pay shareholders. And most does not benefit the local
economy. Most Maui's top hotels are owned by billionaires and multi-national
corporations. The profits go to Wall Street and into the pockets of billionaires like Larry
Ellison, Bill Gates, Michael Dell, and Saudi Arabia Prince Al Waleed bin Talal, just to
name a few.

Hotels are not always staffed by local people. There are not enough locals to staff the
hotels we have now. So, hotels are importing and recruiting mainland workers to come
here to fill these positions. Hotels bring in mainland managers and even international
staff to fill senior positions. And they're not always training them ... The visitor industry
is also underpaying their local workers, so local people working in this industry cannot
support their families long terms and many residents are forced to leave Maui.
Increasing the number of hotels and visitor accommodation is a bad idea. By capping
the number of accommodations, we're actually supporting all of the hotels we have
now, and, because there is supply and demand. When we cap the hotel numbers, we
increase demand, and we can help them to charge higher prices. And so, they can
afford to pay higher wages to their local workers, The visitor industry in Hawaii is
currently underpaying its workers. The average for a hotel housekeeper is $14 to $15
per hour, whereas the high cost of living in Maui makes the minimum livable wage more
like $20 to $25 per hour. Meanwhile, Bill Gates makes $456,625 per hour.
There are better ways to support the local economy than building more hotels. Local

construction companies. We need to ensure that hotels are staffed by Maui locals, and

strongly in favor of the visitor accommodation moratorium. It was a brilliant idea initially
put forward by Counciimember King, and then carried on by Vice-Chair Rawlins-
Fernandez.

by members of the public, which is management of tourism. As we've heard from
lobbyists in the past, the industry does not have intentions of curbing their growth or
stopping. And we've heard those same entities discouraging your attempts in the past
at tourism management, some who don't even reside in this County.
So, this is important, because despite the fact that our economy did take a hit during
the pandemic, tourism has rebounded, even with just U.S. based visitors. A lot of
tourism management does affect our quality of life as residents here in Maui County,
from our ability to access beaches and camping resources, to something as mundane
as our daily commute. I support the resolution referenced in CR 22-41 to go through
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 32
the proper channels, so that the caps and the specifics can be ironed out, and

step of managing overtourism.

Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 34
CHAIR LEE: Members? Member Kama, and then Member Sugimura.
COUNCILMEMBER KAMA: Thank you, Chair. And thank you, Ms. Abdul, for being here.
You know, there was a testimony earlier by Justin Hughey. And he said that his
recommendation, cause he was so passionate about what you folks do, that he would
want everybody to sign up on your list. So, do you have a list that's ongoing? And how
many people are on it? And would you be able to accommodate if everybody got on
that list?
MS. ABDUL: Thanks. That's a really great question. In order to get on our qualified buyer
list, each family or person must go through our four-step process, which is initially
finding out about our program, because it is leasehold and not everybody wants
leasehold property. Then they also have to get pre-qualified. So, you know, that they
are prepared for homeownership, financially. They also take an 8-hour HUD approved
class about financial literacy and also how to maintain and keep your homes in good
condition. And then, meet with us and go through the exact terms of the ground lease,
so there are no surprises, no misunderstanding.
Right now, we have just about 150 people on our list. But that doesn't mean that every
time a house comes up, 150 people are trying to buy it. The last house we just closed
out in Lahaina, thanks to all of you, there is a new teacher and his family that have
moved in. There were 24 families of that 150 that were interested enough to sign up,
take a look at the house. And as it turned out, they went through all of the steps, and
there were 11 families that wanted to buy this one house.

CHAIR LEE: Good morning, Albert.
MR. ALBERT PEREZ. MAUI TOMORROW [testifying on Committee Report Nos. 22-39 &
22-41: and Bill Nos. 77 (2022) & 78 (2022)1:
Good morning, Chair Lee. Happy Earth Day, everyone. Albert Perez, Maui Tomorrow,
and I'm testifying on several items. First one is Bills 77 and 78, Ma'alaea Mauka. Maui
Tomorrow strongly supports funding for acquisition of the Ma'alaea Mauka lands.
Protection of these lands will ensure that cultural and historic resources are preserved,
provide for a natural hazards mitigation, and will create the opportunity to expand
access to open spaces, and the Lahaina Pali trail.
You know, Maui Tomorrow's mission includes preservation of open space, and
promotion of ecologically sound development. And we have always maintained that
this land should remain undeveloped in order to protect the health of the lands makai
and the waters of Maalaea Bay. It's well-suited for preservation and not other, not
housing, especially. It lies at the base of steep slopes that lead up to the wind farm,
and is a natural floodplain for numerous gulches that carry stormwaters down to the
ocean.
The Maui County 2006 Scenic and Historic Resources inventory identified the views
from Honoapiilani Highway across this parcel as being of high value. In, in past years,
much destruction has been caused by large stormflows passing through these lands,
especially after major fires that leave bare soil exposed. Culverts become clogged,
mud ends up on the highway, and there are major brown water events that have had
a cumulative detrimental impact on Maalaea Bay.
So, we appreciate the collaboration of Maui Nui Marine Resources Council, and DLNR.
They have strategies to mitigate the impacts of those floodwaters, and to better
understand the high-volume drainage impacts in the area. This acquisition would
eliminate ongoing pressure to urbanize these lands and would provide an opportunity
to prevent siltation of the waters that are popular for fishing, recreation, humpback
whales, and as I learned this morning, limu. So, glad to hear that. So, I hope that you'll
support that funding.
For Committee Report 22-39, helicopters and noise abatement areas, we support
adoption of these resolutions, which seek to protect the quality of life for our residents.
It's well-known that. . . contributes to many health concerns including stress, anxiety,
depression, high blood pressure, heart disease, and many other health problems.
Citizens all over Hawaii have been fighting the intrusion of aircraft noise for decades.
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 48
But neither the County nor the State has jurisdiction in this area. The Federal Aviation
Administration has control of the skies. But they're mainly concerned with air safety
and commerce. They're not concerned about noise unless they're directed to, and
these resolutions are exactly the right solution. They will put pressure through our
Federal government on the FAA to pay attention to our concerns. And I, I urge you to
pass these resolutions.
Finally, Committee Report 22-41. We urge you to support Resolution 22-70, which
would refer to the planning commissions and advisory committees a bill to cap the
number of new visitor accommodations in Maui County. People often talk about supply
and demand, and we can use that here to our advantage. When we cap the supply on
existing visitor accommodations, they will become more expensive. And this is a good
thing. They'll be able to pay their workers more without increasing the impacts of
overtourism on our community. We already have more than enough hotel rooms, time
shares and other transient accommodations. The economic fallout from the pandemic
related tourism shutdown showed us how vulnerable our economy was and remains to
visitor industry slowdowns. Capping visitor accommodations is the least that we should
be doing. And it's one of the most important things we can do to protect our quality of
life.
If this resolution does not pass, the visitor accommodations moratorium will expire, and
the building of these visitor accommodations will be able to resume. So, please, send
this bill to the planning commissions and the advisory committees, so they'll be able to
have a chance to deliberate the merits of the bill and send their recommendations back
to the Council. There'll be plenty of opportunity for people to testify and express their
opinions during that process. The main group that's been fighting tourism caps is the
hotel developers. They make their money by continuing to lower our quality of life with
more and more tourists. Let that industry go somewhere else and let's build housing
for residents, residents instead. This bill will not reduce the number of hotel jobs. Let's
not forget the lessons of the pandemic shutdown, that we want to stop further growth
of tourism and invest in diversifying our economy so that we will be more resilient next
time. Mahalo.
CHAIR LEE: Madam Clerk, are there any questions?  Idon't see any. Thank you, Albert.
MR. PEREZ; Aloha.

Kai Nishiki, testifying on my own behalf. Government leaders, politicians, tourism

campaign talking points.
We have all seen the media coverage of our beaches completely covered in tourists,
thousands of rental cars clogging our roadways. We see camper vans taking over our
shorelines. But most importantly, we have personally experienced, we, we feel the
hope extinguished to ever own a home, feel our quality of life negatively impacted by
the relentless onslaught of tourism gone wild. This common-sense legislation to
combat the chaos and destruction that unfettered tourism is causing is much needed.

at current levels. Councilmembers have pointed to the need to diversify our economy,
providing training and educational opportunities to our workforce. And this legislation
actually supports that goal. Voters are paying attention. It's election season, to see if

COUNCILMEMBER KAMA: Thank you. Chair, it is my honorto recognize this group of Maui's
outstanding future storytellers for their success at the 2022 STN National Convention
media competition. Storytellers open up worlds of possibility with words and imagery.
They allow us to connect with your journey and expand our own understanding of the
world around us.
To this end, the Student Television Network, founded in 1999, provides a forum for
student broadcasters and teachers to share ideas, ask questions, and learn from
professionals in the industry. I would like to express my deep appreciation to all the
parents, teachers, and mentors, who supported these students and helped them
develop the technical skills and critical thinking needed to achieve such recognition at
the national level.
I am so happy and proud to have the opportunity to celebrate the Maui Nui winners at
the 2022 STN National Convention media competition, and we congratulate them on
their accomplishments. So, congratulations students and teachers, and best wishes
for continued success in broadcast journalism, film, and media, as you continue to tell
your stories in such effective and creative ways. And one day, I hope that this could
be an economic engine for our Maui County. Chair,  Irespectfully ask for the Members
full support of my motion. Thank you.

Committee met on April 4, 2022, to discuss Bill 30 (2022). These bills would amend
the Fiscal Year 2022 Budget, Appendix A, Part II, to add an appropriation under the
Affordable Housing Fund for the extension of Wela Street, including street lighting
signage, striping, and landscaping, for the Kilohana Makai Project, in the amount of
$825,000.
Your Committee noted that Ordinance 5151 (2020) changed the zoning for this
property from Open Zone to R-1 Residential, and included a condition to extend Wela
Street to Kilohana Drive.
The Department of Housing and Human Concerns material costs have increased
exponentially in the past year, and every increase makes it harder to complete the
project. The Department does not want to pass these additional costs onto buyers.
The Managing Director said that this is not the first time the County has assisted with
costs of zoning condition for a 100 percent workforce housing project.
Your Committee voted 8-0 to recommend passage on first reading of Bill 30 (2022). I
respectfully ask for the Members continued support of this. Mahalo, Chair.

Management for 60 South Church Street Building Renovations.

repairs.
Your Committee discussed the duration of the renovations. The Department of
Management said they anticipate Departments will be able to move into the building in
approximately one year.
The Budget Director also said the Administration is seeking Federal funding to assist
with the building renovations. This budget amendment will allow the Department to
proceed with a RFP process and other purchases. But if Federal funding is received,
the Budget will be amended to recognize the additional funding and reduce the amount
of bond funding.

Bill 35 (2022); Bill 36, GDI (2022); Bill 37 (2022), Bill 38, CD1 (2022). I respectfully

COUNCILMEMBER SUGIMURA: Your Infrastructure and Transportation Committee met on
March 22, 2022, to discuss the following. And this resolution was presented by Keani
Rawlins-Fernandez, Resolution 22-71, intended to urge the Federal Aviation
Administration. FAA, to move effectively regulate helicopter operations in Maui County.
And Resolution 22-71 [sic], which was my resolution, intended to: 1) urge the
assistance of Hawaii's Congressional delegation to have the FAA hear citizens'
concerns and work to address aircraft noise complaints; and 2) urge the State
Department of Transportation and the Mayor to independently or jointly establish a
community roundtable on aircraft noise with the FAA.
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 110
At this meeting your Committee discussed community concerns regarding aircraft
noise and flight paths into and over Maui County, particularly helicopter noise
disturbances over Waihee Valley, East Maui, and Molokai, and commercial aircraft
noises over Haiku, Maalaea, South Maui, and Molokai.
Your Committee discussed communication efforts \with the FAA to address these
concerns, resulting in the FAA recommended the initiation of a roundtable, taskforce,
or ad hoc committee to engage the local community and address related concerns.
Your Committee also noted the support of U.S. House of Representative Congressman
Kaiali'i Kahele for both resolutions.
Your Committee supported adding language to Resolution 22-71 to recognize that the
silence of Haleakala is recognized as a treasure, and to urge the National Park Service
to discontinue tour helicopter operations over Haleakala National Park.
Your Committee supported adding language to urge the FAA to issue a rule to regulate
and reduce helicopter overflights and attendant noise disturbance over nearby
communities, similar to Title 14, Code of Federal Regulations, Part 93, New York North
Shore Helicopter Route.
Your Committee further supported amending Resolution 22-74 to clarify the mapping
of noise abatement areas for the Island of Maui, identify current flight paths, and, and
directly urged the FAA instead of the State's Congressional Delegation to adhere to
the mapping noise abatement areas.
Your Committee voted 6-0 to recommend adoption of Resolution 22-71, CD1, and
voted 5-0 to recommend adoption of Resolution 22-74, CD1. I respectfully ask for the
Councilmembers support of the motion. Thank you. Chair.

COUNCILMEMBER PALTIN: Okay, going back to the main motion as amended. Your
Planning and Sustainable Land Use Committee met on March 17, 2022, and
reconvened on March 23, 2022, to discuss a public private partnership agreement
between the State, County, and Waikapu Country Town Project, in this partnership,
Waikapu Country Town would provide additional residential workforce housing units in
exchange for infrastructure improvements by the State and County, hopefully the State
also.
The Committee received the computer-generated presentation from Waikapu Country
Town representatives that outlined the proposed terms of the Agreement, which
included Waikapu Country Town providing up to 213 additional residential workforce
housing units; the County assuming Waikapu Country Town’s traffic impact mitigation
obligations: and Waikapu Country Town being permitted to temporarily connect to the
County's, Kahului Wastewater Treatment Facility that would allow the construction of
the housing units while the County builds the Central Maui Wastewater Treatment
Facility.
Your Committee amended Resolution 22-51 in two ways: 1) requiring Waikapu
Country Town to seek Council approval to revise conditions to the Change in Zoning
and District Boundary Amendment, and one of the modifications that I verbalized, and
Mr. Atherton agreed to, was extending the affordability period of the additional
residential workforce housing units; and 2) to urge the Mayor to exercise reasonable
efforts to secure State funding as the State's participation in the Agreement.
Your Committee supported the concept of government entities partnering with
developers to provide housing for the workforce and the community.
Your Committee voted 9-0 to recommend adoption of Resolution 22-51, CD1. And so,
you know, we signaled for the developer that we're willing to do our part. We
mentioned our one concern that, you know, we wanted to extend the affordability
period from 2.96. And Mr. Atherton was okay with that, if you folks remember. So, I
respectfully ask for the Members support of my motion as amended.

Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 124
By correspondence dated March 17, 2022, Council Vice-Chair Keani Rawlins-
Fernandez submitted to the Committee a revised bill incorporating the TIG's
recommendation and feedback from County Administration and the Department of
Corporation Counsel.
The Committee supported amending the bill to require the Planning Department and
Department of Finance to maintain a list of all rooms or units zoned for transient
vacation rental use to help in streamlining the administration of the caps. And this is
for the A-1 and A-2 properties.
Your Committee amended the proposed resolution by substituting the attached
proposed bill v^ith the revised bill received by correspondence dated March 17, 2022,
from Council Vice-Chair Keani Rawlins-Fernandez.
Your Committee also amended the revised proposed bill to limit the number of rooms
or units zoned for transient vacation rental use to all those allowed for transient
vacation rental use as of January 7, 2022, whether or not they were currently being
used for that purpose.
Finally, the Committee amended the bill to prohibit vehicles from temporarily parking
in all zoning districts if used as a short-term accommodations unless they are allowed
by zoning and the proper permits are obtained.
Your Committee voted 5-0 with four Members excused, to recommend adoption of the
Resolution 22-70, CD1. And I think we received the most written testimony on this
item in support. I respectfully ask for the Members support of my motion.
CHAIR LEE: Alright. Anybody else?
Vice-Chair Rawlins-Fernandez.
VICE-CHAIR RAWLINS-FERNANDEZ: Mahalo, Chair. I speak in strong support of the
motion. Residents have been clear in their demand for immediate Council action to
manage tourism in Maui County. This Council has passed a new tourism
accommodation moratorium, established a Tourism Management and Economic
Development TIG, and this is the natural next step in the right direction.
By maintaining a tourism accommodation, tourism accommodations at the current
level, we can effectively preserve the legally allowed number of short-term
accommodations in zoning districts, while simultaneously addressing the much-
needed prohibition of pervasive vacation rental camper vans taking up residents'
space.
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 125
This legislation was the culmination of well-considered solutions that resulted within
the months of hard work of the Tourism Management and Economic Development TIG,
and one of the many proposals that will be heard by this Council in the coming months.
This particular piece of legislation was expedited for transmission to the various
Planning Commissions, and Committees, Advisory Committees, for their
consideration, and is an opportunity for further community participation.
Once passed, it will end the moratorium intended to be short-lived, intended to be a
short-lived temporary hold on transient accommodation growth, while the promised
permanent solution was developed. And this is the solution. Mahalo, Chair.

Discussion? Vice-Chair Rawlins-Fernandez.
VICE-CHAIR RAWLINS-FERNANDEZ: Members, in the April 4. 2022, Budget, Finance, and
Economic Development Committee meeting, we discussed Bill 46 (2022), "A BILL FOR
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE FISCAL YEAR 2022 BUDGET FOR THE
COUNTY OF MAUI AS IT PERTAINS TO ESTIMATED REVENUES. OFFICE OF THE
MAYOR, ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT PROGRAM, MICRO GRANTS PROGRAM
FOR AXIS DEER MITIGATION; TOTAL OPERATING APPROPRIATIONS; TOTAL
APPROPRIATIONS (OPERATING AND CAPITAL IMPROVEMENT PROJECTS)".
The bill's purpose was to amend Fiscal Year 2022 Budget, allocate 1,500,000 in
additional transient accommodation tax revenues to assist small farmers and ranchers
with mitigation, fencing, and other necessary measures to find relief and protect their
property from feral animals.
The grants will be available to eligible Maui County resident farmers and ranchers with
sustained losses resulting from excessive axis deer population and other feral animals
since July 1, 2021, and would be administered by Lokahi Pacific.
During the April 4 meeting, your Committee expressed support for the purpose of the
bill, but concerns about the bill title being unclear as to the purpose of the funding. The
Administration agreed to submit a new bill with an updated title, which is the bill we are
currently considering. Bill 76 (2022). The purpose of the bill remains the same. I

Discussion, Member Sinenci.
COUNCILMEMBER SINENCI: Thank you, Chair. Bill 54, CD1 establishes qualifications for
the Director and Deputy Director of Agriculture.
In accordance with the County Charter Section 6-4, which states that in addition to
minimum qualifications for administrative heads, as set by the County Charter,
additional qualifications may be expanded by the Council by ordinance.
The qualifications in the bill include minimum experience in ag production, food
distribution systems, and ag programs in Hawaii, also ag-related management and
budgeting, working with various cultural backgrounds, and experience and knowledge
of native Hawaiian sustainable farming techniques. The Director is also required to
research ag sector issues, and collaborate with community experts, and is also
encouraged to attend continuing educational classes.
The bill received extensive community support and was passed unanimously out of
Committee. And the Department of Ag will be established on July 1,2022. And these
qualifications will help guide the Administration during the current recruitment process.
Members, we also added additional positions and funding during our budget
proceedings to further bolster the Department's success. With that, I respectfully ask
for the Members support of my motion.

Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
April 22, 2022
Page 164
CHAIR LEE; Okay. I think we, Corp. Counsel was going to give us a comparison of some
kind.
Keola?
DEPUTY CORPORATION COUNSEL WHITTAKER: Yes. Chair. Thank you, Chair. Before
we do the comparison, the Deputy Clerk has asked that we resolve a possible
confusion regarding how the ballot will list the Charter Commission proposal and the
Council alternative. It'll just take a second.
So, the form of the ballot is dictated by State law, and that's 50-10, HRS 50-10. So,
State law provides that the Charter Commission proposal and the Council alternative
will be listed on the ballot as two separate questions, with an indication that the
alternative is a alternative to the proposal.
The voters will not be choosing between A, B, or  Clike a multiple-choice test. Instead,
the voters will vote "yes" or "no" to the proposal and the alternative. So, that means
that a voter could vote "yes" on both the proposal and the alternative. Of course, they
could also vote "no" to both. So if both the proposal and the alternative get more than
50 percent "yes" votes. Whichever gets the greater number of "yes" votes will prevail.
So, what that means is if the Council does not recall the three alternatives today, they
will appear as second ballot questions, along with the Commission's proposal. In
effect, that means that there could be anywhere between 11 ballot questions, if you
don’t have any alternatives, or 14 ballot questions, with the three alternatives. I know
that was a mouthful. So, in simple terms, the ballot questions are always yes/no, not
multiple choice.
So, Richelle has prepared a redline between the Charter Commission's proposals and
the alternatives that she could pull up for your review.
CHAIR LEE: Member Sinenci, you have a question of Keola?
COUNCILMEMBER SINENCI: Thank you. Chair. Yeah, so we can rescind only the Council's
proposal.
DEPUTY CORPORATION COUNSEL WHITTAKER: That's right, so-
CHAIRLEE: Yeah. Yeah.
DEPUTY CORPORATION COUNSEL WHITTAKER: That's right, just the three Council
proposals that were not adopted.

DEPUTY CORPORATION COUNSEL WHITTAKER: A blank vote does not count. So, a
blank vote does not count as a "no". So, when you’re looking at whether a proposition
passes, you're just looking at "yes" and "no" votes. So, if you get 99 "no" votes and
100 "yes" votes, it passes no matter how many blank votes there are.
COUNCILMEMBER SUGIMURA: Okay. Thank you.

nine, eleven-members; nine by Council, two by the Mayor, not requiring confirmation
by any other body.
And then, two officers were removed from going through the independent nomination
board process. And that would be the County Clerk and the Auditor. So, the
independent nomination board would be involved with, in the Council's version,
selecting, vetting and proposing members to boards and commissions, and also the
Corporation Counsel and Prosecuting Attorney.

On Apr 22,2022, at 4:17 PM, David Dorn <daviddorn808@gmail.com> wrote:
Testimony in support of limiting the number of NEW visitor accommodations in Maui
County 4/22/2022, Agenda Item; CR 22-41
“Konichiwa”, and Happy Earth Day, my name is David Dorn (not a lobbyist),
I agree with Lucienne from Sierra Club on all her points, We need to provide the extra
funding to protect the Ma'alaea Watershed, and we need to support our upcountry
farmers to better control feral animals (deer etc.) in the Mauka Watershed.
I also support the adoption of resolution 22-70. We need more Homes, not Hotels.
And We need to Manage Tourism so it benefits Maui County Locals, the “moms and
pops”.
Maui County already has more than enough hotel rooms, timeshares, and other
transient accommodations. We have more hotel rooms per-capita than Oahu, and we
are more tourist-dense than Waikiki.
Maui Now has up to One Tourist for every 2-3 locals. Far exceeding our limits, and our
levels set in the Maui Island Plan. This is totally unsustainable. And there are not even
enough locals to work these hotels, so Hotels are importing more people to work in
these hotels.
Hotel workers brought in from the mainland are buying up all of our “workforce and
affordable housing”, and there is nothing to stop them.
The 2-year Visitor Moratorium is actually benefiting the housing industry as construction
is focussing on home-building and other kinds of construction. This is actually helping us
fill the need for more housing for locals. But, this is only a temporary solution to Maui's
housing crisis. This bill for a “Cap on Tourist Accommodation” could similarly help our
construction industry to focus on the kinds of projects that will actually benefit local
families, such as building more housing and schools.
Many Hotels on Maui are owned by huge mainland corporations. The majority of Profits
from the Hotel industry goes offshore to pay shareholders, and most does not benefit the
local economy.
FYI, Maui’s top hotels are owned by Billionaires and Multinational Corporations, the
profits go to Wall Street. And into the pockets of billionaires like Larry Ellison, Bill Gates,
Michael Dell, and Saudi Arabian Prince Al-Waleed bin Talal, just to name a few.
Hotels are not always staffed by Local people. There are not enough local workers to
staff the hotels we have now, and there are not enough local workers to staff new hotels.
This causes hotels to recruit mainland workers to come to live on Maui and fill these
positions.
1
Hotels bring in mainland managers and even international staff to fill senior positions.
They are not always training and recruiting local people.
Not enough locals to staff these hotels: The visitor accommodation industry is importing
a large number of their workforce.
The visitor industry is also underpaying their local workers. So local people working in
this Industry cannot support their families long-term. So many residents are forced to
leave Maui.
Increasing the number of Hotels and Visitor accommodations is a bad idea. By capping
the number of accommodations, we are actually supporting all of the Hotels we have
now. It is supply and demand. When we cap the number of Visitor accommodations we
keep demand high. Then they can charge higher prices, and they need to be able to
charge higher prices in order to pay their local workers a sustainable living wage.
*Local Maui residents who work in this industry need to be able to buy homes and pay
rents in Maui’s competitive housing market.
The visitor industry in Hawaii chronically underpays its workers. We need to support
local unions that are fighting Hotels to get a decent wage. The average wage for a hotel
housekeeper on Maui is still only $14-15 dollars per hour. The high cost of living on
Maui makes the minimum livable (sustainable) wage on Maui to be at least $20-25 per
hour. Meanwhile Bill Gates makes $456,625 an hour.
There are better ways to support the local economy (than building more hotels):
Hotels are not always built by local contractors and these projects go to lowest
bidders. We
can change that.
We need to stop big construction jobs going to off-island and mainland
companies.
We need to ensure that our building projects go to Local Builders who use local
labor. This is
how we support our local construction industry.
We need to ensure that Hotels are staffed by Maui Locals. And that Hotels hire
Hawaiians to fill
all levels of staffing positions.
We need to ensure that Hotels pay their workers a decent living wage that is
sustainable for
the Cost of living here in Hawaii.
We need to raise taxes on forign-owned Hotels and Visitor accommodations
2
● We need to raise taxes on absentee landlords that are converting homes to
TVRs, and Condos to
● Time Shares.
Please recommend adopting this resolution, so that it can be properly deliberated and
debated by the planning commission. The planning commission deserves to hear the
input from the whole community and stakeholders in this important issue that could
determine the fate of the local economy and all the community who lives here.
Aloha.

Testimony in support of limiting the number of NEW visitor accommodations in
Maui County 4/22/2022, Agenda Item: CR 22-41
To:
Cc:
Subject:
Testimony in support of limiting the number of NEW visitor accommodations in Maui County
4/22/2022, Agenda Item: CR 22-41
“Konichiwa”, and Happy Earth Day, my name is David Dorn (not a lobbyist),
I agree with Lucienne from Sierra Club on all her points. We need to provide the extra funding to
protect the Ma'alaea Watershed, and we need to support our upcountry farmers to better control feral
animals (deer etc.) in the Mauka Watershed.
I also support the adoption of resolution 22-70. We need more Homes, not Hotels. And We need to
Manage Tourism so it benefits Maui County Locals, the “moms and pops”.
Maui County already has more than enough hotel rooms, timeshares, and other transient
accommodations. We have more hotel rooms per-capita than Oahu, and we are more tourist-dense
than Waikiki.
Maui Now has up to One Tourist for every 2-3 locals. Far exceeding our limits, and our levels set in the
Maui Island Plan. This is totally unsustainable. And there are not even enough locals to work these
hotels, so Hotels are importing more people to work in these hotels.
Hotel workers brought in from the mainland are buying up all of our “workforce and affordable
housing”, and there is nothing to stop them.
The 2-year Visitor Moratorium is actually benefiting the housing industry as construction is focussing
on home-building and other kinds of construction. This is actually helping us fill the need for more
housing for locals. But, this is only a temporary solution to Maui's housing crisis. This bill for a “Cap on
Tourist Accommodation” could similarly help our construction industry to focus on the kinds of projects
that will actually benefit local families, such as building more housing and schools.
Many Hotels on Maui are owned by huge mainland corporations. The majority of Profits from the Hotel
industry goes offshore to pay shareholders, and most does not benefit the local economy.
FYI, Maui’s top hotels are owned by Billionaires and Multinational Corporations, the profits go to Wall
Street. And into the pockets of billionaires like Larry Ellison, Bill Gates, Michael Dell, and Saudi Arabian
Prince Al-Waleed bin Talal, just to name a few.
Hotels are not always staffed by Local people. There are not enough local workers to staff the hotels
we have now, and there are not enough local workers to staff new hotels. This causes hotels to recruit
mainland workers to come to live on Maui and fill these positions.
Hotels bring in mainland managers and even international staff to fill senior positions. They are not
always training and recruiting local people.
Not enough locals to staff these hotels: The visitor accommodation industry is importing a large
number of their workforce.
The visitor industry is also underpaying their local workers. So local people working in this industry
cannot support their families long-term. So many residents are forced to leave Maui.
Increasing the number of Hotels and Visitor accommodations is a bad idea. By capping the number of
accommodations, we are actually supporting all of the Hotels we have now. It is supply and demand.
When we cap the number of Visitor accommodations we keep demand high. Then they can charge
higher prices, and they need to be able to charge higher prices in order to pay their local workers a
sustainable living wage.
*Local Maui residents who work in this industry need to be able to buy homes and pay rents in Maui’s
competitive housing market.
1
The visitor industry in Hawaii chronically underpays its workers. We need to support local unions that
are fighting Hotels to get a decent wage. The average wage for a hotel housekeeper on Maui is still
only $14-15 dollars per hour. The high cost of living on Maui makes the minimum livable (sustainable)
wage on Maui to be at least $20-25 per hour. Meanwhile Bill Gates makes $456,625 an hour.
There are better ways to support the local economy (than building more hotels);
● Hotels are not always built by local contractors and these projects go to lowest bidders. We can
change that.
● We need to stop big construction jobs going to off-island and mainland companies.
● We need to ensure that our building projects go to Local Builders who use local labor. This is
how we support our local construction industry.
● We need to ensure that Hotels are staffed by Maui Locals. And that Hotels hire Hawaiians to fill
ail levels of staffing positions.
● We need to ensure that Hotels pay their workers  adecent living wage that is sustainable for the
Cost of living here in Hawaii.
● We need to raise taxes on forign-owned Hotels and Visitor accommodations,
● We need to raise taxes on absentee landlords that are converting homes to TVRs, and Condos
to Time Shares.
Please recommend adopting this resolution, so that it can be properly deliberated and debated by the
planning commission. The planning commission deserves to hear the input from the whole community
and stakeholders in this important issue that could determine the fate of the local economy and all the
community who lives here.
Aloha.

To: Honorable Alice Lee, Chair and Members of the Maui County Council
From: Tamar Goodfellow, President, Maui Health Foundation
Re: Support for "CR 22-85, authorizing the disposition of real property to the
Maui Health Foundation and for waiver of outstanding real property
taxes" and Support for "CR 22-84, authorizing the disposition of real property
to the dba Na Hale 0 Maui and for waiver of outstanding real propel^Itaxes^ XI
nro
oAloha Chair Lee, Vice Chair Rawlins-Fernandez and Council Member^^ b.,
rr.
My name is Tamar Goodfellow. I serve as the volunteer President ofJthe Mai^
Health Foundation, a 25 year old non profit organization whose sole mission is’
to support the highest quality of health care at Maui Memorial Medical
Center, Kula Hospital and Lanai.
3:^
00
iTl
O
My devotion to our hospital and to health care on our island stems from a
personal passion to save lives here on Maui. With only one acute care
hospital, Maui Memorial is the place that each of us, our family members, our
friends, and our visitors will go in a life threatening medical emergency. I want
it to be the best.
In addition, housing for the working members of our community, teachers,
police officers, fire fighters, and so many others is equally critical if we are to
maintain a safe, healthy and successful community.
This is why I am asking for your support for the transfer of these lots.
*  Each year our only hospital cares for more than 40,000 patients,
including those on medicare, quest/medicaid, the underinsured and
uninsured. No one is turned away.
*  Maui Memorial has the second busiest emergency department in the
state of Hawaii, second only to Queens.
*  Quality of care directly correlates to Care Providers. Island wide, we are
short hundreds of doctors, nurses, technicians and aides. This shortage of
Care Providers is a growing issue nationwide, but Maui is particularly
challenged with recruiting and retaining Care Providers. Right now the hospital
is short staffed in every department.
*  The single biggest barrier to recruiting and keeping Care Providers on
Maui is the lack of housing at all income levels.
*  The County of Maui owns 55 lots in Maui Lani, walking distance from
the hospital. The Maui Health Foundation is asking for your support to
transfer in fee simple, 16 of those lots to be held in perpetuity by the
Foundation for Care Provider housing.
*  Our program will be modeled after Na Hale 0 Maui. The land will be
held in perpetuity by the Foundation. Homes will be built by a home builder,
and sold to care providers at leasehold rates, meaning less the value of the
land, and the restriction that future buyers must also be care providers. This
makes the homes, first, available nearby the hospital, and second, attainable.
*  Ail healthcare providers are eligible. (They do not need to be hospital
employees). If applicants are below the 140 AMI, they will be directed to
NHOM. If they are above 140 AMI, they will be asked to get pre-quaNfied for a
mortgage and be part of the Foundation lottery.
*  Selection criteria will be weighted by the following criteria: greatest
community need (as determined by annual healthcare survey); Maui or Hawaii
born Care Provider seeking to return home; current resident Care Provider
seeking to purchase their first home.
*  Home buyers will own the home and improvements, but not the land.
They will pay a monthly leasehold fee, determined to cover the management
costs of the program/property. (Though not yet finalized, we have begun a
dialogue with Na Hale 0 Maui asking them to act as the property manager for
the 16 Maui Health Foundation homes funded by the lease rent to not only
cover their management costs but also further their mission.)
*  There are deed restrictions. When a home owner sells, there will be a
shared appreciation where the home owner will retain at least 50% of any
equity in the home, (less the land value). The formula will be modeled after
NHOM. Because the value of the land is deducted from any appreciation of
the property, the price point for the homes can remain stable. The seller must
sell to another qualified Care Provider.
*  We have been asked why the County should support housing for
Physicians and Nurses who earn a substantial salary, versus community
members with greater financial need. Simply put, we need housing for
everyone, but the ability to attract and retain Health Care Providers is
becoming critical on Maui. Doctors may become wealthy over time, but
initially have a difficult time qualifying for a mortgage because of their high
education debt and lack of a guaranteed level of income, while they start and
build their practice.
This property has a long and sordid history. Resolutions 22-84 and 22-85 are
proposed as Phase 1, creating the opportunity to do something positive with
the 33 lots that are not controversial, and address the critical need for
workforce housing. Phase 2 includes 19 additional lots adjacent to Palama
Street, that involve long standing issues (Wall, fill, drainage, etc.) that need to
be resolved by engaging the Palama Street residents.
It should be noted however, that an existing archeological study conducted by
Dr. Six shows no Iwi Kupuna sites on the property. If Iwis hold be found during
the home development process, we are committed to stop work and follow all
appropriate protocols. In addition, the State Department of Health issued a
letter stating that the mill mud used as fill on the lots has been tested and
cleared for use, and finally, the County of Maui Department of Water has
issued verification that water and meters are available for the 33 lots.
There is a critical need for housing for Care Providers that may save your life,
or that of someone you love. And a need for workforce housing for all
members of our community I am happy to try and answer any questions you
might have, but before I close, I would like to share a quote from Dr. Rafael
Oania, a Board Certified Anesthesiologist, born and raised on Maui.
"It is a dream of mine to be able to come home to Maui to practice medicine.
After years of training in New York City, I was ready to bring my talents back to
Maui. However, the harsh reality of the housing crisis in Maui has steered me
away from this dream. It's sad to think that a well paid physician isn't even
able to afford or find an affordable home in Maui. It Is a concern that not only
affects the recruitment of physicians but the prosperity of the entire working
class and families who are at risk of being unable to live a reasonable life on
the island that they have called home for generations."
Mahalo for considering the passage of Resolution 22-85 and 22-84.

Subject; Committee Report 22-35 regarding Resolution 22-85, Authorizing the Disposition of Real
Property to Maui Health Foundation
Dear Chairperson Lee and Council Members;
Na Hale 0 Maui, in collaboration and support of Maui Health Foundation (MHF), respectfully
requests your approval of Resolution 22-85 regarding the disposition of 16 lots in the Fairways in
Maui Lani and to MHF and to waive any outstanding real property taxes.
Our community is at the tipping point in Health Care. Maui has a critical shortage of medical
personnel, especially those who practice crucial specialty areas, Maui desperately needs
excellent Physicians and other medical professionals, to provide the highest level and quality of
care for our community. Maui Memorial Medical Center is short-staffed in every department.
There is a shortfall of care providers island-wide and Doctors, nurses and other medical
personnel. Many of those wonderful caregivers who went above and beyond the call of duty to
serve our community during the covid pandemic are now moving away because of the high cost
of living, and Maui's shrinking rental market in one of the highest costs places to rent or buy and
live in the country. We must take steps now to reverse this alarming trend with a iong-term,
damaging impact on the delivery of life.-saving medical care for us all.
We need access to excellent medical care and potential emergency medical treatment. Without
essential physicians and other important health care providers, Maui residents are forced to fly
to Oahu or beyond for medical treatment. Some specialties are not permanently available in the
state, forcing patients and families to relocate to the mainland where specialists are more readily
available on a daily basis.
The need for housing at affordable prices occurs at every level of our community. This continues
to frustrate the Maui Hospital Foundation's mission to provide the highest quality of health care,
the inability to attract and keep great physicians and medical personnel, because of the Maui
housing market.
Na Hale O Maui strongly supports affordable and workforce housing initiatives and
developments. We believe working in collaboration with MHF makes perfect sense for this
project and our community. NHOM's program can accommodate workforce households that
earn up to 140% of AMI, Including health care providers like nurses, therapists and others.

Subject; Resolution 22-84, Authorising the Disposition of Real Property for Housing and Land
Enterprise of Maui, dba Na Hale 0 Maui and for Waiver of Outstanding Real Property
Taxes
Dear Chairperson Lee and Council Members:
We write today to request your kokua to authorize the disposition of 19 lots (17 finished lots and
2 driveway lots) located in the Fairways in Maui Lani to Na Hale 0 Maui (NHOM) and waive any
outstanding and unpaid real property taxes.
We were surprised and delighted when the Budget Finance and Economic Development (6FED)
Committee unanimously approved Resolution 22-84 during the April 4, 2022, meeting. This
demonstrates the Council's understanding of the crucial need for affordable and workforce
housing for island families,
The median price of a single-family home in Maui reached $1,177,500 at the end of March 2022.
The astronomical price of homes has a disproportionate impact on low- and moderate-income
families, forcing many to reconsider their future in Maui. Unfortunately for our community, the
brightest residents with the most potential to help Maui thrive, are leaving for more affordable
mainland cities where the cost of living is substantially lower and housing, whether for rent or to
own, are affordable and attainable. This is borne out,by recent U.S. Census Bureau data that
places Hawaii as the third largest population decline out of all 50 states.
Statistics show that workers have to earn $60 - 70 per hour for 40 hours per week in order to
afford a single-family home at these prices. UHERO found that service workers in Hawaii earn
about $17 an hour. Limiting household expenses to 30% of gross monthly income would mean
working 33 hours per day - clearly an impossibility. The median income, workforce family simply
cannot afford or qualify for a median income home.
Hawaii faces an annual shortage of more than 1,000 teachers each year. We have a critical
shortage of medical personnel. Crucially needed physicians continue to decline to move to Maui
because of the availability and cost of housing. Supporting medical personnel face the same
dilemma. Businesses cannot find workers, forcing some to permanently close their doors. These
are some of the symptoms of our cost of living and housing challenges.
In 2021 the US Bureau of Economic Analysis, Regional Data, found that Honolulu was one of the
most expensive metropolitan areas in the country, with a cost of living 13% higher than the
190 N. Church Street, P.O. Box 1829, Wailuku, HI 96793 ● Ph. 808.244.6H0* Fax 808.244.6115 ●www.nohaleomaui.org
Alice Lee, Chair
Maui County Council
Page 2
average metropolitan area. The high cost of living in Hawaii makes it virtually impossible to save
a down payment, especially one substantial enough (20% or $200,000 on a $1 million dollar
home) to avoid Private Mortgage Insurance of roughly $30 - $70/month per $100,000 of
mortgage. Most low- to moderate-income families cannot qualify for a mortgage on the median
priced home.
What does this mean for us? We face a steady loss of our keiki, mo'opuna, family, friends and
neighbors. They have finally given up on the high cost of housing and living here. They move to
mainland states with lower costs of living, more affordable rents and for-sale homes that are
both affordable and attainable. Our families and the entire community are diminished with
each additional loss of 'ohana.
What can we do? This is our kufeana; our responsibility. We can take action now to help our
workforce and community by approving Resolution 22-84 that will provide some badly needed
and truly affordable workforce homes. Working collaboratively with the County of Maui, for-
profit and nonprofit developers and contractors, lenders and the community, we can provide
more critically needed homes for our families.
The 17 Fairway at Maui Lani house lots and 2 driveways (a total of 19 lots), the subject of
Resolution 22-84, are a golden opportunity to take unproductive lots and create Community
Land Trust homes for income-qualified island families-that will remain truly affordable in
perpetuity, homeowner after homeowner, generation after generation. Each additional home
we provide will improve and change the lives and opportunities for another island family.
Together we can make a real difference for Maui Nui.
Housing and Land Enterprise of Maui, dba Nd Hale  0Maui (NHOM) is a grassroots, membership-
based Nonprofit 501 (c) 3 Community Land Trust, established to secure qnd preserve o
permanent supply of affordable housing alternatives for low- and moderate-income households
in Maui County- Our focus is truly affordable homes in perpetuity for workforce families earning
between 80%-140% of the Area Median Income (AMI) for Maui County.
We ask for your kokua to authorize the disposition of 19 lots in the Fairways in Maui Lani to Na
Hale Q Maui (NHQM) and waive any outstanding real property taxes.
Mah^o piha for your support of affordable workforce housing and the Community Land Trust!

Dear Maui County team,

Aloha,
As a long time resident of Maui (moved here from Honolulu in 1973) I have seen many changes - and lots of inevitable
growth. We count on our local government to manage it with strong consideration given to the rights and well being of
our residents.
In the last 6 months or so, there has been an apparently unregulated proliferation of camper vans, rented to visitors.
This by-passes all County planning - and existing short term rental rules and taxation. Our parks and beaches are already
being overwhelmed by the sheer number of visitors: there is certainly no room camper vans.
I have been relieved to see enforcement of Maui's short term rental regulations - although there are still many illegal
units (1 think that the fines are a pittance compared to the profits.)
BUT, camper vans should be entirely banned! We are not like New Zealand - with miles of empty land and
accommodations for RV camping. We are already overwhelmed by the sheer number of visitors on our beaches and
parks: we must have them protected, as well as our at residential neighborhoods!
We are counting on you: no half-way measures which would create an enforcement nightmare.
Sincerely,
Stephanie Austin

We have been in the rental business on Maui for over 14 years, and have a\ways paid our Ge and Tat
and Prop Txs in full.
We have an excellent reputation for serving our customers, and only now have begun to recover from
our covid shutdown.
We do not understand the cap proposal, but if it is to limit the number of legitimate rentals in our area
then we have a very serious problem with the proposed legislation.
Why would county Maui want to limit the very source of revenue that is the life blood of our beautiful
place here in the sun?
Make no sense to us, and it makes no sense to any one else in the rental business in the County of
Maui.
Sincerely yours,
Lawrence Burke, Sole Prop.
250 Hauoli Street NO. 109
Wailuku

Re: Testimony in Opposition to the Proposed Transient Accommodation Cap,
Resolution 22-70, CDl (Committee Report No. 22-41)
Dear Chair Lee and Councilmembers:
My name is Rob Gunthner, and I am the Area Vice President, Resort Operations — Hawaii for
Hilton Grand Vacations (“HGV”). HGV owns and operates the Maui Bay Villas Resort in Kihei,
and the Ka’anapali Beach Club in Ka’anapali. We write to express our concerns regarding the
Proposed Bill Amending the Comprehensive Zoning Ordinance Relating to Transient
Accommodation Caps (the “Proposed Cap”). In brief, the Proposed Cap will not effectively
address the problem of illegal short-term rentals and will be detrimental to the community and
legally-operating transient accommodations, an economic engine for Maui.
The Proposed Cap seeks to permanently freeze the number of rooms and units used for
transient vacation rentals at the number in use as of January 7, 2022. If enacted, the Proposed Cap
will present an impractical and short-sighted solution to managing tourism. The Proposed Cap will
not reduce visitor’s demand for travel to Maui. The Proposed Cap will exacerbate the shortfall of
legal transient accommodations, and will effectively incentivize illegal short-term rental use. This
incentive lures visitors out of resort zones and into the communities where short-term rentals
(whetlier legal or illegal) are located. While illegally operating short-term rentals can and should
be regulated, a permanent cap on transient accommodations is not the appropriate means to do so
as it will not directly address illegally operating short-term rentals. Legal operators of transient
accommodations should collaboratively work with the County to find solutions that keep tourists
in resort zones and out of illegal short-term rentals.
Mahalo for the opportunity to provide testimony on tlie Proposed Cap. We ask that the Council
not refer the Proposed Cap to the Maui Planning Commission.
Veiy tmly yours,
AobGunmoer
Atm VP-H«svat
Rob Gunthner
Hilton Grand Vacations Waikoloa Resorts
69-699 Waikoloa Beach Drive^ Waikoloa, HI 96738
T 808-881-3000 f 808-881-3034 w hiitongrandvacations.com

Aloha County Clerk and Yuki Lei,
My name is Aubrey Hord and I am a resident of Pukalani. I have lived on Maui since 1991. It sounds like we are at the
point where we need to voice our concerns about the dramatic increase in Camper Vans and similar RV's/5th Wheelers
being brought over from the mainland and be used as vacation rentals.
We knew someone would probably try to do this with the high room rates and crack down on illegal vacation rentals.
The damage these camper vans and similar vehicles are currently causing on the island as well as the potential for future
damage (environmental, social and cultural) is obvious. The increase in camper vans parked on public beaches nightly
has skyrocketed and the rubbish and human waste left behind is disgusting, let alone the fact that they are unpermitted.
They prevent residents from legally fishing and camping as well as potentially damaging turtle nesting sites. The
individuals renting these vehicles most likely have little to no knowledge of Hawaiian culture, values or environmental
stewardship of the land as shown in social media posts. A very valid concern for the residents of Hana and Kahakuloa is
the larger vehicles are not able to fit on the narrow Hana Highway or Kahekili Highway.
I would highly recommend that we ban the use of camper vans, RV's and 5th wheelers from being used as overnight
lodging, let along being used as vacation rentals.
Mahalo,
Aubrey

Aloha,
My name is Kim and I am writing to leave my public comments on Resolution 22-70.
I am strongly apposed to this resolution and I feel the council is focusing in the wrong direction. The below link will lead
you to a study which shows that Hawaii has some of the toughest housing regulations in the United States.
https://www.mauinews.com/new5/local-news/2022/04/uhero-hawaiis-housing-regulations-among-toughest/
Why is the council not focusing their attention on easing these restrictions, which will allow for more affordable housing
for Maui residents?
Our family business manages vacation properties in the Kapalua Resort. We have been in business for almost 40 years. If
this resolution goes forward, many of the properties on the resort will no longer be designated for short term vacation
rentals. These properties are in no way affordable and it is ludicrous to propose the idea that they are.
In turn, companies like ours will go out of business, our employees with lose their jobs, and the trickle down effect will
be catastrophic for Maui. Our vendors, restaurants, activities, stores and more will all feel the loss and they too will
suffer.
We have paid millions in taxes over the years. If you put companies like ours out of business, and reduce tourism, where
is all the money going to come from to support important programs such as affordable housing?
How will residents who lose their jobs be able to afford their homes, let alone a home or villa in a resort? What industry
will be waiting for Maui residents and our employees when they are our of work?
This proposal is not logical and the numbers do not add up. But I don't think it is meant to be logical. I feel there is great
animosity to the tourism industry and sadly it seems like members of the council are willing to take it down by any
means necessary, even if it's at the expense of Maui residents.
Focus on affordable housing and those who have illegal vacation rentals. There is no other industry at the time that can
provide jobs and a tax revenue like Hawaii's tourism industry. It is not logical to reduce that industry drastically without
something to take its place.
Thank you for your time.
Kimberly N Johnston

industry to flourish over resident needs. The last thing we need is for these camper vans to take

Testament regarding Shortterm rental caps
From:
Sent: ZIIZZ APR 20 PH 06

OFFICE OF THESubject:
COUNTY CLERK
I You don't often get email from kohlmolo@gmail.com. Learn why this is important
Aloha
My name is kohl Naehu I live and is from the island of Molokai and currently have 3 rentals under my ownership and
management that is under transit accommodations, as a active resident of Hawaii
I'm all for short term rental cap to limit the use of short term rentals on Molokai and in Maui county.
The state of Hawaii agreed decades ago on allowing a certain percent or visitors to the island's based on each islands
resident count this visitor percent or count has been grossly exceeded due to political greed and has made Hawaii less
attractive as a tourist destination, due to mass vehicle and human traffic, due to pollution and due to less than
reasonable cost of services and goods.
I strongly support tourism in Hawaii because we as kanaka have a lot to share, teach and set the example for the rest of
America and set the base for the rest of the world on how to live, treat each other and the earth, tourist dollar is the
easiest and most economical way for Hawaii to stand with the rest of the countries of the world financially in the
positive.
I feel short term rental properties should be only allowed in the proper zoned and in a well staffed location for visitor
safety and to promote recurring visits. ( example hotel zoned condo resort zoned properties).
Mahalo
Kohl Naehu

Re: Grant of 19 Lots in Central Maui to Housing and Land Enterprise of Maui, dba Na Hale O
Maui
Resolution 22-84
Dear Honorable council.
My family and I ask that you support Na Hale O Maui's request for the Grant of 19 lots in
Central Maui, for the purpose of building homes for low- and moderate-income workforce
households who have completed the Na Hale O Maui  4Step Program.
Affordable housing is very important to me and my family especially with the rising cost of
homes here on Maui. We are a household with a moderate-income, where we don't qualify for
any government assistance and with the rising cost of homes still can't afford a home for our
family. We have lived with family and are now renting. With homes, my family's future of
being homeowners one day seemed unrealistic with median houses priced over a million
dollars. Also with overpricing conditions with rent, we end up paying the majority of our
income towards it.
When my family heard about Na Hale O Maui and how they help families like ours to become
homeowners, we couldn't believe it and signed up as soon as we could. We believe having
more affordable housing on Maui makes it more possible for families like ours, members of the
workforce and local community to obtain their dreams of homeownership. We truly feel Maui is
an amazing place to raise our family, like we have been and our kupuna have before us.
Na Hale O Maui has helped 12 families into their own homes in Lahaina in 2020. My family has
our own dreams of owning one of these homes as well. Your support for this grant will help
make our dream of homeownership a reality!
Mahalo for your time and help.
Stacey Pianas
45 Kapi Lane Apt 9-201
Wailuku, HI 96793

COUNCIL OF THE COUNTY OF MAUI
Councilmember Alice L. Lee, Council Chair
Councilmember Keani Rawlins-Fernandez, Council Vice Chair
NOTICE OF HEARING
Friday, April 22, 2022 at 9:00 am. Online Via Blue Jeans
In Support of Bill 59, CDl (2022), RELATING TO THE PLUMBING CODERe:
Aloha Chair, Vice Chair and Council Members;
Mahalo for the opportunity to testify in support of Bill 59, CDl (2022) which updates the
current plumbing code for Maui County.
Chartered in 1919, the Plumbers and Pipefitters UA, Local 675 is one of the oldest organized
labor unions in Hawaii and one of three licensed' skilled-construction trades, steeped in a rich
history as one of Hawai'i's construction-industry pioneers.
The Plumbers and Pipefitters UA Local 675 appreciates and thanks this Committee, its Staff and
the Department Public Works for giving us the opportunity to provide input and comments
regarding this important Bill.
Local 675 supports the County's efforts to maintain current plumbing codes by adopting the
2018 published edition of the Uniform Plumbing Code as amended, as doing so increases
efficiencies in the built community, reduces costs and assists in preserving Hawaii's most
valued resource (water).
Adopting Bill 59, CDl (2022) most importantly supports the stated purpose^ and underlying
intent to safeguard public health, safety, and welfare by ensuring that plumbing systems are
designed and constructed according to minimum industry standards by qualified and licensed
professionals.
Mahalo for the opportunity to testify in support of this important measure.
^ Bill 59 (2022), Relating to the Plumbing Code, Section 101.3 Purpose. This code is an ordinance providing
minimum requirements and standards for the protection of the public health, safety, and welfare.

April 20, 2022
Testimony for CR 22-41
Position: In support of
Aloha! Please prohibit camper vans on Maui (and all of Hawai'i) for these reasons:
1. They do not pay Transient Accommodations Tax (TAT) and therefore do not contribute to our economy except to
enrich the vehicle owner renting out these vans
2. They take up valuable resources, crowding out beaches and campgrounds, also while not contributing to our
economy. They are also competing for resources and supplies by buying out supermarket shelves of produce and
products. These are resources that residents have to compete with tourists for.
3. When they camp randomly in residential areas or areas not meant for camping because there are no restroom
facilities, they are literally shitting and peeing by the side of the road next to their vans.
4. Each island has a carrying capacity that has been far exceeded due to the unrestrained allowance of tourism. We have
more and more homeless, who are not allowed to sleep in their vehicles, while tourists in these vans are.
They are using and consuming our resources while paying no tax whatsover.
Is this really in the true spirit of Malama 'Aina?
Is this really what we want the future of Hawaii to be? Unrestrained access for tourists while our local residents and the
state pay the real price?
Gabriel Riela-Enoka
Full time Hawaii resident, residing on Oahu and tax payer

Aloha,
I am a Big Island resident who has reported several camper vans and giant RVs that are illegally being used as "tents" at
Spencer Beach on the Big Island. While camping is allowed through obtaining a permit campers must be in a designated
camping area. A parking lot is not considered a camping area. Unfortunately your colleagues at the Hawaii County Parks
and Recreation are at odds w the Hawaii County Police who have to enforce these rules. One rule is that people are not
allowed to sleep overnight in their cars. A camper van/RV is considered a vehicle. Yet so many tourists who want to fly to
Hawaii on the cheap and avoid staying in a hotel, don't know this is NOT allowed. Furthermore, people who renovate
and retrofit cars for camping also do not know this is not allowed.
An additional problem is the trash. I pick up so much trash that it is getting to be an issue. I have even pulled out a
Hummer out of the ocean. Trash would be cut by limiting camper vans on the premesis.
Currently Councilman Tim Richards of South Kohala's District 9 where Spencer is located, is working on a plan to limit the
issuing of permits on all types of camping, including camper vans. I have suggested to him that permits should be issued
to local Big Island residents FIRST.
Please do not be like your colleagues at Hawaii County Parks and Recreation in issuing camping permits to visitors in
camper vans.
Mahalo.
Jada
Jada Rufo
