Aloha. I am writing in regards to camper van regulation. I have been a resident of Maui for 30 years
who works in the medical field. I work at the hospital and the private office setting. Recently I had
the ability to head to the beach with my sister. We went to thousand peaks. We parked and had a
nice local man approach us. He informed us we were lucky to get a spot. He said usually it is filled
with camper vans and cars but since the county usually comes to empty trash on Thursday everyone
cleared out until they were finished. I had been noticing more and more of the vans on the island
which is quite disturbing. Sure enough the next week I was driving to Lahaina for an early morning
whale watch and when driving by thousand peaks there was van after van parked at the beach. This
will make it very difficult for residents to be able to enjoy the beach when they have the day off and
have the opportunity to enjoy the day with their family. Tourism has reached a point where the island
cannot sustain the numbers. I still do not understand why as tax payers we are paying so much to
promote Maui. Maui spends much more than the other islands and it is completely unnecessary to
spend such an enormous amount of money.
Anyway back to the topic at hand. Please regulate this burgeoning industry that has such a negative
effect on the local residents.
Thank you for your time and your desire to do something about this issue.
Aloha. Lisa Schlichting. Haiku, Maui

Testimony for CR 22-41 // Position: In Support of
From:
Sent: 2P/2APr;2i A^!0●07
To:
Subject: 1  i
h::;TY clerk
I You don't often get email from luanne.teoh@gmail.com. Learn why this is important
April 20, 2022
Testimony for CR 22-41
Position: In support of
Aloha! Please prohibit camper vans on Maui (and all of Hawai’i) for these reasons:
1. They do not pay Transient Accommodations Tax (TAT) and therefore do not contribute to our
economy except to enrich the vehicle owner renting out these vans
2. They take up valuable resources, crowding out beaches and campgrounds, also while not
contributing to our economy. They are also competing for resources and supplies by buying out
supermarket shelves of produce and products. These are resources that residents have to compete
with tourists for.
3. When they camp randomly in residential areas or areas not meant for camping because there are
no restroom facilities, they are literally shitting and peeing by the side of the road next to their vans.
4. Each island has a carrying capacity that has been far exceeded due to the unrestrained allowance of
tourism. We have more and more homeless, who are not allowed to sleep in their vehicles, while
tourists in these vans are.
They are using and consuming our resources while paying no tax whatsovere.
Is this really in the true spirit of Malama ‘Aina? Tourists are literally shitting all over the islands
because they are living out of vans.
Is this really what we want the future of Hawaii to be? Unrestrained access for tourists while our local
residents and the state pay the real price?
Luanne Teoh
Full time resident, employer and tax payer
Maui, Hawaii

M AUICHAMBER OF COMMERCE
VOICE OF BUSINESS
Maui County Council
Alice Lee, Chair
Keani Rawlins-Fernandez, Vice Chair
Members of the Maui County Council
Testimony in opposition to Bill 24, CD1. FD1 (2022)
Aloha Chair Lee, Vice Chair Rawlins-Fernandez and members of the Council
The Maui Chamber of Commerce would like to testify in opposition to Bill 24, CD1, FD1 (2022)
relating to maximum building heights in the B-2 community business district, B-3 central business
district, and P-1 and P-2 public/quasi-public districts.
The Chamber does not support legislation that creates non-conforming structures. This bill as it
originally stood exempted Maui from these height limits and therefore did not create many, if any, non-
conforming structures on Moloka’i or Lana’i. But, Councilmember Paltin’s approved amendment to
include the West Maui Community Plan area in the restrictions will likely create a number of non-
conforming structures.
The Chamber would like to point out the strong opposition by the State of Hawaii Office of Planning &
Sustainable Development as well as Hawaii Housing Finance and Development Corporation from their
testimony at the committee hearing.
For these reasons we respectfully request that Bill 24, CD1, FD1 (2022) be filed..
Sincerely
Pamela Tumpap
President
To advance and promote a healthy economic environment
for business, advocating for a responsive government and
quality education, while preserving Maui’s unique
community characteristics.

MAUICHAMBER OF COMMERCE
VOICE OF BUSINESS
Maui County Council
Alice Lee, Chair
Keani Rawlins-Fernandez, Vice Chair
Members of the Maui County Council
Testimony in support of Committee Report 22-35
Aloha Chair Lee, Vice Chair Rawlins-Fernandez and members of the Council
The Maui Chamber of Commerce would like to testify in support of Committee Report 22-35 which
recommends the adoption of resolutions 22-84 and 22-85. These resolutions authorize the waiving of
outstanding property tax balances and the disposition of 19 lots at the Fairways at Maui Lani and the
waiving of outstanding property tax balances and the disposition of 16 lots at the Fainways at Maui Lani.
We are all aware that there is a crucial need for affordable and workforce housing for island families.
Hawaii is now the State with the third largest population decline according a recent calculation by the
U.S. Census Bureau.
No Hale O Maui (NHOM) is a grassroots, membership-based Nonprofit 501 (c) 3 Community Land
Trust, established to secure and preserve a permanent supply of affordable housing alternatives for low
and moderate-income households in Maui County. Their focus is truly affordable homes in perpetuity
for workforce families earning between 80%-140% of the Area Median Income (AMI) for Maui County.
The Chamber strongly supports affordable and workforce housing initiatives and developments. We
have faith that by working collaboratively with the County of Maui, developers and contractors, lenders
and the community, Na Hale O Maui can provide more critically needed homes for our families. The 17
Fairway at Maui Lani house lots and 2 driveways (a total of 19 lots) are a golden opportunity to take
unproductive lots and create Community Land Trust homes for income-qualified island families that will
remain truly affordable in perpetuity, homeowner after homeowner, generation after generation.
Maui Memorial Medical Center (MMMC) is the only place on this island that can provide critical,
lifesaving care to our residents and our visitor. For those with the most critical needs, there is often no
other option. They do not have the time to delay treatment or the strength to make the trip to another
island to receive care.
Today, MMMC is short 75 registered nurses, despite hiring every single graduate of the University of
Hawaii Maui College, every year. Per MMMC, the Operating Room has lost a couple of nurses and a
surgical tech with housing and affordability as the primary reason for their resignation. They have been
unsuccessful in recruiting viable candidates with housing as the primary reason offers are being
declined.
To advance and promote a healthy economic environment
for business, advocating for a responsive government and
quality education, while preserving Maui’s unique
community characteristics.

Testimony with Comments on CC22-93
Aloha Chair Lee, Vice Chair Rawlins-Fernandez and members of the Council
We would like to offer the following comments with regards to the Charter Commission’s response to
the proposed amendments offered by this Council
Proposal 1 Commission accepted Council’s alternative to eliminate the proposal. This proposal will not
appear on the ballot. AGREE
Proposal 3 Commission rejected Council’s alternative to eliminate this proposal. Proposal 3 will appear
on the ballot. AGREE
Proposals 2, 4, 5, 6, 7, 9 Commission accepted Council’s alternatives, which alternatives will be
incorporated into the Commission’s report to the County Clerk and will appear on the ballot. AGREE
with 2 (we are working on a video that may help), 4, 7 and 9 (with comments previously shared). We
do not agree on 5 & 6 as we feel these should be eliminated (based on comments previously shared).
Proposals 8, 10, 13 Commission rejected Council’s alternatives. As described below, Council may
consider recalling these alternatives. DISAGREE with proposals 8 (recommended other ways to
address this), 10 (as the system is fair and balanced it is about treatment, which is a big concern) and
13 (removing the caps is deeply concerning; there should be known caps).
Proposal 11 Commission voted to remove this proposal from the ballot. It will not appear on the ballot.
AGREE
Proposal 12 Council offered no alternative. This proposal will appear on the ballot. DISAGREE (with
comments previously shared)
Sincerely
Pamela Tumpap

Re: Testimony in SUPPORT of RESOLUTION 22-65 - APPROVING COST ITEMS WITHIN BARGAINING
UNIT 1 REPRESENTED BY THE UNITED PUBLIC WORKERS FOR FISCAL YEARS 2022, 2023, 2024, AND 2025
Chair Lee, Vice Chair Ra\A/lins-Fernandez, and Members of the Council:
The United Public Workers, AFSCME Local 646, AFL-CIO ("UPW") is the exclusive bargaining representative
for approximately 14,000 public employees, which includes blue collar, non-supervisory employees in
Bargaining Unit 1 and institutional, health, and correctional employees in Bargaining Unit 10, in the State of
Hawaii and various counties. The UPW also represents 1,500 members in the private sector.
UPW strongly supports Resolution 22-65, which approves the cost items for the Bargaining Unit 1 Collective
Bargaining Agreement between the Employer and UPW for the fiscal period from July 1, 2021 to June 30,
2025 for included employees of the County of Maui.
The approval of this resolution will help to ensure that our Bargaining Unit 1 members in the County of Maui
will receive the necessary funding for the respective cost items in this new agreement.
Thank you for the opportunity to provide testimony.
Sincerely,
Kalani Werner

Aloha e Maui County Clerk,
Please forward the below testimony to the Planning & Sustainable Land Use Committee regarding CR 22-41.
Dear Chair and Members,
The last two years have produced some interesting  &unintended situations for our island community. The pent up
demand for travel has seen incredible demand for any type of rental vehicle. First it was car sharing service and now it
has mushroomed into RV's, minivans converted into 'campers', pop-up tents on all types of vehicles and potentially soon
5th wheelers. We do not have legal camping/RV parks like one might see on the mainland.
This rapid rise in alternative lodging causes many concerns. 1) Revenue - they are not paying TAT, MCTAT and
RPT. They are also not paying the County or State to park on the roadsides or beaches (which is already illegal). 2)
Environmental Concerns - human waste, litter are some initial concerns. 3) Malama Hawaii - This is not the respectful
traveler we need. This traveler is not treating our home with cultural and environmental respect.
Mahalo for your efforts to address this quickly troubling issue. I trust that we can get ahead of this problem sooner
rather than later.
Mahalo,
John
